Hebei's Financial Deficit 104

Difficulties in Drafting New Budget, Various Agencies to Reduce Administration

Tianjin Correspondence: The Hebei Provincial Finance Department convened a financial meeting on the 24th to discuss the drafting of the 24th year budget. Those attending were Zhāng Hòuwǎn, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Hú Yuánhuì, Director of the Department of Construction, Wèi Jiàn, Secretary-General of the Provincial Government, and Zhèng Dàorú, Director of the Department of Education, who was absent due to other matters and sent Section Chief Shū Zǐqí as his representative. Lǔ Mùtíng, Director of the Department of Finance, was unable to attend due to a foot ailment and sent Sūn Xiàngqián, the secretary-director of the department, as his representative. The meeting was chaired by Wèi Jiàn. After the meeting, Wèi Jiàn explained the general situation of the province's financial revenues and expenditures. It was stated that the total deficit in the province's final accounts for the 22nd year was over 5 million yuan. Although revenues this year have shown a slight improvement, due to the abolition of excessive taxes and miscellaneous fees, it is estimated that there will still be a deficit of over 1.4 million yuan. The province's sources of revenue have been exhausted. Furthermore, at the National Financial Conference convened by the Ministry of Finance this year, it was decided that all provinces should completely abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous fees by the end of the 23rd year. A large portion of the province's revenue is from regular taxes, but 40-50% still involves excessive taxes and miscellaneous fees. If the ministry's order is followed, it will not only affect tax revenue but also potentially create problems for the progress of general administration. Therefore, it is necessary to find ways to make up for the losses on the one hand and to carefully review and reduce expenditures on the other, so as to balance revenues and expenditures and prevent the budget for the 24th year from running into difficulties. When the province convened the provincial administrative conference, the Ministry of Finance sent expert Wēng Zhīyóng to the province, who proposed a plan for reorganizing the province's finances and drafting a new budget. The plan was based on the actual expenditures of the province's Party and government agencies in the 22nd year as a standard, regardless of previous surpluses or deficits, to be used as the basis for drafting the budget for the 24th year. In a desperate situation, the province can only implement this plan to maintain operations. However, with this budget, the expenditures of various agencies in the province will be reduced by a certain amount. Agencies have no other choice but to implement austerity policies. How to reduce personnel and administrative expenses is also a very important issue. Therefore, the meeting was convened to decide on the standards for drafting the provincial budget and to discuss how to change the budgets of various agencies, etc. After the report, the attendees discussed the matter in detail for several hours. Each department stated that the budget they had prepared had already been reduced to the minimum. If further reductions were made, it would be necessary to conduct a detailed review of what should be reduced and what should be cut, re-compile the budget, and then submit it for discussion. A decision was made to adjourn the meeting at that time. It is reported that the province's tax revenues this year in the counties south of Hebei Province have either suffered from famine, drought, and floods, or have not recovered from last year's locust plague, resulting in unsatisfactory revenues and many delays in paying land taxes. In the counties of the war zone north of Hebei Province, due to being within a special sphere of influence, rural areas have gone bankrupt, resulting in a certain reduction in revenues. Compared to these areas, only the central counties are doing relatively well, with an average of 70-80% of taxes paid. As for the abolition of excessive taxes and miscellaneous fees in the province, apart from the first phase that has already been implemented, the second phase will have to be postponed to next year for gradual implementation due to the lack of funds to compensate for the losses. (December 24th)

Headquarters Inspection Team Arrives in Wuhu 105

Inspecting Rural Cleanup Matters in Southern Anhui

Wuhu Correspondence: The inspection team from the Nanchang Headquarters for inspecting the rural cleanup and rehabilitation affairs in the bandit suppression areas, led by Director Lǐ Wànlǐ, has arrived in Wuhu yesterday with member Chén Kèchéng to inspect the rural cleanup matters in various counties in southern Anhui. A joint meeting was convened at the Commissioner's Office, attended by Commissioner Wáng Zhùrén, Public Security Bureau Chief Wáng Zōngfén, Deputy Commander of the Security Forces Hú Pèigēng, as well as the heads of the Public Works Bureau, the Construction Commissioner, and various district heads. Director Lǐ immediately instructed on the implementation according to the regulations of the Headquarters inspection team. Regarding the security forces, they must be built into a strong and effective force. The militia must enhance their self-defense capabilities. The defenses must prevent bandits from infiltrating. Food distribution must ensure that no one in the jurisdiction is displaced. The pao-chia [neighborhood watch] system must be strictly organized so that bad people cannot hide. Cooperatives must complete the cooperative organization of all districts in the county. Popular education must ensure that all illiterate adults receive popular education. Traffic must complete the main roads in the county, connect the counties and neighboring telephones, repair and guard bridges, eliminate all illegal and excessive taxes, and improve the financial organization. After the meeting, the following resolutions were made: (1) Coordination between the pao-chia system and education: the urban areas' joint pao-chia system will be divided into several educational districts, and each district must set up a school, with the principal responsible for urging school-age children in the district to enroll and for popular education. (2) In rural areas, each joint pao will set up a school, with the principal serving concurrently as the director, and jointly responsible for popular education. (3) Graduates from the militia cadres training program will be used to fill the positions of militia captains in the joint pao, and will also be responsible for assisting the pao-chia chiefs in compiling and checking household registrations. Their allowances will be paid from the pao-chia funds. (4) Each school principal in the education district and the pao-chia district must jointly conduct a drill once a year. (5) The district public office will select one person with military experience to serve as a district officer and be responsible for commanding the militia training. (6) Standard of defense deployment: Wuhu and Dangtu will rush to build city defense bunkers, and the lines of fire must be connected. The city walls of Chaoxian, Wuwei, Tongling, Fan, Nanling, and Liuan counties must be intact, and bunkers must be built as appropriate. The militia in the urban area of Wuhu must be under unified command and training, and designated guarding sections. (7) Promoting cooperatives: A joint office of cooperative instructors from various counties will be established in the Commissioner's Office, and the Provincial Cooperative Committee, the China Foreign Famine Relief Committee, the Shanghai Bank, and the Industrial Bank of China will jointly organize cooperatives in various counties and provide loans. It is planned to set up more than one hundred cooperatives in each county. (8) Public Security Issues in Wuhu City: Capable household registration police officers will be selected, and household registration will be checked and personnel registration will be handled based on the pao-chia system. The Wuhu City Public Security Bureau Chief will be responsible for the public safety of Wuhu City. (9) Rectification of the Security Forces: Based on the guiding principles for improving the security system, the spirit of education and training of the committee, the commissioner will supervise and order various counties to complete the work within one month and await inspection. After the inspection team completes its work in Wuhu, it will go to Huizhou and various counties in southern Anhui to conduct on-site inspections. The Anhui Provincial Government has specially assigned personnel to assist at any time. (December 25th)

Fujian Relief Committee Prepares to Provide Emergency Relief to Western Fujian 106

Chén Péikūn Inspects Disaster Situation in Liancheng, Xiamen Copper Coins Surge in Price, Have Slightly Fallen Back

Xiamen Correspondence: The Fujian Provincial Relief Committee, organized by the provincial government and chaired by Chén Péikūn, recently traveled to western Fujian with Kāng Shàozhōu, consultant to the Security Office, carrying 40,000 yuan in cash, to inspect the disaster situation in the bandit areas and provide relief. Chén and others departed from Zhangzhou on the 14th and returned to Zhangzhou on the 22nd after completing the inspection. They issued a statement on the results of the inspection, stating that they took a car to Longyan on the 14th, stayed for four days, went to Pengkou on the 18th, and then to Hetian, 40 li from Changting. Because the road from Hetian to Changting was not finished, the road was very rugged, so Kāng Shàozhōu went to Changting to inspect and distribute relief. Chén returned to Pengkou and went to Liancheng to inspect for two days, and returned to Yan on the 21st and arrived in Zhangzhou on the 22nd. Liancheng had been occupied by bandits for a long time, and many houses and villages were destroyed, leaving only broken tiles and ruined walls. The county government building was leveled and is now used as a training ground for troops. Nine out of ten residents have left, with only a few men who have recently returned after the recovery. Outside the city and in the countryside, there are more women. Strong men have either died or fled. There is a severe shortage of rice, oil, and salt. Local people and the garrison have jointly formed a cooperative, which has an oil and salt sales office, so there is no worry about supply. In terms of finance, the county chamber of commerce currently issues paper money, which can be exchanged for Bank of China notes. As a result of the inspection, it was concluded that in addition to Wenfang and Pengkou, which have been heavily affected by the war and are in dire need of emergency relief, the rest should focus on work relief. Upon returning to the province, a report on the inspection will be prepared, and a plan will be submitted to the province for implementation. When we arrived in Yan, rice prices in Wenfang and Pengkou were very high, so we first sold 2,000 yuan of rice at a subsidized price. As for rural finance, there is a branch of the Four Provinces Farmers Bank in Xiamen, and it has been decided to establish a branch in Liancheng. Also, Chén telegraphed the provincial government in Yan, stating that after Changting was recovered, the population was increasing daily, and there was a shortage of rice and salt. He had purchased 1,000 bags of rice from Zhangzhou and requested the Pacification Headquarters to allocate ten trucks to transport them to Longyan and then to Changting to provide relief. As for salt, 100,000 catties of salt have been allocated from the Shima Salt Affairs Bureau, to be transported by merchants to Changting, Liancheng, and Ninghua for sale at a subsidized price. Also, in the newly recovered bandit areas of Liancheng, Changting, Ruijin, and Huichang, the Red Bandits searched for and took away all the cash when they fled westward. After the recovery, as people gradually gathered and merchants became more prosperous, there was an unusual shortage of cash. However, the bandit areas were extremely poor, and transactions rarely involved silver dollars. As a result, merchants from Zhangzhou and Xiamen competed to transport copper coins to the recovered bandit areas to make a profit. In the past two weeks, a large amount of copper coins flowed into Liancheng, Changting, Ruijin, and Huichang, and the price of copper coins in Zhangzhou and Xiamen surged. One Xiamen silver dollar could originally be exchanged for more than 370 copper coins, and one small silver coin (ten cents) could be exchanged for 30 copper coins. In the middle of this month, the price surged wildly. On the 18th, it surged to only 235 copper coins for one silver dollar, a loss of more than 130 copper coins, and 20 copper coins for one small silver coin, a loss of 10 copper coins, an increase of one-third or more. The reason for this is that merchants are hoarding and speculating. By the 24th, it had begun to fall to 24 copper coins for one small silver coin and 270 copper coins for one silver dollar. (December 24th)

The Ministry of Finance's Review of National Finance: Past and Future (Continued) 107

▲ Shandong Province: Located in the heart of the Jinpu Railway, Shandong is rich in resources and its people are prosperous. The revenue and expenditure for the 20th year of the Republic were 10,063,000, 12,460,000 in the 21st year, and 12,700,000 in the 22nd year. There have been no significant changes overall, and the finance can be considered stable. Starting this year, the first batch of provincial taxes that hinder central revenue, such as the tobacco tax and other taxes that involve double taxation, such as the meat trade and opera tax, and those that hinder transportation, such as excessive loading, vehicle, pedestrian, and boat taxes, totaling 109,728 yuan, as well as miscellaneous local taxes in various counties amounting to 31,174 yuan, will all be abolished in July. The second batch includes a total of 602 types of provincial and county miscellaneous taxes, totaling 197,556 yuan, which will be abolished from December 1st.

▲ Hebei Province: Due to years of war and disasters, Hebei has suffered a continuous stream of misfortunes. As a result, the rural areas have declined, commerce has stagnated, and financial difficulties are more severe than in the past. This year, the first financial conference was convened, and representatives from the Hebei Provincial Department of Finance attended. After detailed discussions, the estimated shortfall in revenue and expenditure is approximately 1,710,000 yuan. However, the provincial authorities are still able to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes amidst extremely difficult financial circumstances. The implementation is rapid. (1) Labor service, with an annual amount of 191,003 yuan, miscellaneous taxes with an annual amount of 60,010 yuan, and miscellaneous income with an annual amount of 31,045 yuan. Of the above three items, the amount belonging to the provincial treasury is slightly more than 165,580 yuan, and the remainder is allocated to various counties. There are 90 types of miscellaneous taxes belonging to the county, such as livestock transit tax, with an annual amount of 273,302 yuan, all of which will be abolished uniformly from July 1st. Furthermore, in 51 counties where the surcharge on land tax exceeds the regular tax, it has been reduced to within the regular tax. In 32 counties, including Cangxian, the surcharge is equal to the regular tax, resulting in a total reduction of 799,000 yuan. The remaining 19 counties, including Wen'an, still need to reduce 596,000 yuan, and strict orders have been given to reduce it within the deadline.

▲ Shanxi Province: Due to the supply of troops stationed in the province and the occurrence of droughts and floods in recent years, Shanxi Province is at risk of having revenue not meeting expenditure. The local finances of various counties are also extremely chaotic. After the resolutions of the financial conference were announced, in accordance with the central government's intention to care for the people, the names of harsh levies and forced apportionments, such as those based on grain, mu, or household, and those differentiated by military service, education, and construction, have been strictly reduced or abolished. In addition, among the various taxes, the decision was made to first abolish the four items that levy taxes on goods and involve harsh details, such as egg white, egg yolk, walnut, peach kernel, pig and sheep small intestine, and cattle and sheep bone horn.

▲ Shaanxi Province: Since the founding of the Republic, Shaanxi Province has been plagued by warfare, and there have been no peaceful years. In addition, natural disasters have been frequent, and the vitality of the province has been depleted. The provincial treasury has debts of more than 10 million. Currently, the Department of Finance is implementing a strict austerity policy, eliminating embezzlement, and formulating a reorganization plan. As for the case of abolishing excessive and miscellaneous taxes resolved by the financial conference, Shaanxi Province is also determined to implement it in accordance with the central government's intention. The amount of abolished taxes has reached more than 100,000 yuan. It is also planned to reduce or exempt 61 types of local taxes, totaling more than 280,000 yuan.

▲ Suiyuan Province: Suiyuan Province is located in a remote and barren area, and the people are struggling. Starting this year, it is planned to waive all outstanding taxes from the 17th and 18th years of the Republic, amounting to more than 390,000 yuan. In addition, redundant institutions will be merged, which can save 340,000 yuan per year. The budget for the security regiment will be reduced by more than 100,000 yuan in the first year, striving to gradually achieve a non-salary system. In addition, by eliminating extravagance and harsh disturbances, the burden on the people of Suiyuan can be reduced by at least 700,000 yuan per year. Regarding the taxes in Suiyuan Province that should be abolished, the following are included: Koubei Mongolian Salt Food Household Tax, Tax, Coal Tax, Freight Tax, Oil Tax, Wugongba Road Work Tax, Pig Bristle Tax, Public Debt Additional Charcoal Half Tax, Boat Escort Fee, Boat Escort Additional Office Fee, Vegetable and Grass Boat License Fee, Nursery Fee, and other 13 types, with an annual reduction of more than 210,000 yuan, which are limited to be abolished from August 1st to December 1st. Regarding the taxes and fees in other counties that should be abolished, those that have already been abolished include miscellaneous taxes and land tax surcharges in Guisui, Xinghe, Helin, Qingshui, Hexian, Guyang, Jining, and Liangcheng, totaling 45,586 yuan.

▲ Chahar Province: Chahar Province is originally a barren area. Since the Zhangjiakou-Kulun road was blocked, commerce stagnated, and the rural economy was in distress. In addition, due to frequent misfortunes in recent years, the finances of various counties are increasingly unable to make ends meet. Under these circumstances, the provincial authorities are still able to separately abolish 25 types of miscellaneous taxes, totaling 20,879 yuan, and cancel the number of apportioned funds in various counties, totaling 511,779 yuan. It is also planned to implement the reduction and exemption of labor service in various counties from January 1st of the 24th year of the Republic, totaling 11,876 yuan, a land tax surcharge of 91,187 yuan, and provincial local donations of 219,000 yuan.

▲ Ningxia Province: Ningxia is located in a remote border area, and commerce is sluggish. Border defense is important, and military affairs are increasingly urgent, with huge military expenditures. Although the various military and administrative expenses have been reduced to the extreme, there is still an annual deficit of more than 1.5 million yuan. However, the provincial government is still able to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes in three phases in accordance with the time limit set by the ministry. The first phase includes nine types: rice purchase tax, livestock tax, salt camel tax, cart camel tax, land mu smoke lamp tax, and head burden tax, totaling 124,776 yuan annually, which will be abolished from August 1st. The second phase includes two types: post-disaster fines and special cigarette tax, totaling 301,140 yuan annually, which will be abolished from November 1st. The third phase includes one type: temporary maintenance fee, totaling 344,660 yuan, which will be abolished on January 1st of the 24th year of the Republic. ▲ Gansu Province: Due to the excessive burden of military expenses, Gansu Province's finances are exhausted. As a result, levies are collected locally, with numerous items. Recently, the province has been trying to reorganize in order to comply with the resolutions of the financial conference. Among the taxes, the most urgent and important of those that are similar to excessive and detailed taxes are: the abolition of the mill tax, which is approximately 40,000 yuan per year, the camel tax, which is approximately 120,000 yuan per year, and the tea tax, which is approximately 130,000 yuan per year. As for land tax, the most unfair burden is the field grain, and the amount of tax is often several times higher than the people's grain. It is now being limited to change the field to the people, and after implementation, it can be reduced by approximately 290,000 yuan per year.

▲ Qinghai Province: Since the abolition of the likin in the 20th year of the Republic, Qinghai Province's revenue has decreased significantly. In addition, due to the war in the Northeast, most of the fur has not been shipped, and the tax revenue has been insufficient. The accumulated deficit over the years has reached 4,290,000 yuan. Since the financial conference, Qinghai Province, in accordance with the central government's intention to reorganize land tax, plans to abolish the surcharge amount of more than 14,600 yuan. As for the excessive and miscellaneous taxes of various provincial assets, efforts are also being made to abolish them.

▲ Guizhou Province: Guizhou Province is located in the center of the southwest and has always been known as barren. Since the order was given to abolish the likin in the 20th year of the Republic, the province has suddenly lost a huge amount of revenue. In addition, disasters have been frequent, and the annual revenue and expenditure are extremely different. Although various counties have never had a land tax surcharge, the collection of donations and taxes is complicated. Since the order was given to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes, it has been thoroughly reorganized, and it has been decided to abolish them in three phases, with two months as a period, from July 1st to the end of December of the 23rd year of the Republic. The first phase has already abolished more than 16,000 yuan of excessive and miscellaneous taxes, and efforts are still being made to abolish all excessive and miscellaneous taxes in the province by the end of the year.

▲ Fujian Province: Incidents occur frequently in Fujian Province, and tax revenue deviates from the norm. Various counties often solicit requests from local groups and arbitrarily add surcharges to the provincial tax. Recently, the Department of Finance has actively reorganized, and the first batch has abolished the most excessive and miscellaneous taxes, such as jasmine, chicken, duck, and goose taxes, totaling more than 10,000 yuan per year. The second batch will abolish 12 types of excessive river taxes in the Jiulongkou area of Zhangzhou and 98 types of miscellaneous local taxes in various counties, with an annual amount of more than 83,600 yuan.

▲ Guangdong Province: Since the implementation of the three-year administration plan, Guangdong Province has made the most efforts to reduce and abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes. Those belonging to the provincial treasury revenue have been reduced by more than 80 types, with an annual amount of more than 115,000 yuan, all of which will be abolished separately in August of this year. In addition, there are 1,680,000 yuan of likin-like revenue, which are planned to be abolished uniformly by the end of July of next year. ▲ Guangxi Province: Guangxi Province's finances have been reorganized the most vigorously, such as (1) dividing provincial and county taxes, (2) unifying revenue and expenditure, (3) strictly implementing budgets and final accounts, (4) summarizing the names of taxes, (5) equalizing the tax burden, and (6) abolishing transit taxes. The effect of implementing this for a year has been quite remarkable. As for the various excessive and miscellaneous items that have been abolished, the number of those that can be verified is more than 430,000 yuan per year.

▲ Sichuan Province: Sichuan Province's defense areas have not yet been unified, and there is no investigation into the finances. In addition, the latent spread of communist bandits is enough to affect the stability of the finances. Currently, the provincial authorities are trying their best to plan. If there is anything that can be done, they will proceed accordingly in order to alleviate the suffering of the people.

▲ Yunnan Province: Yunnan Province has abolished excessive and miscellaneous taxes since the reform of the tax system in the 19th year of the Republic. Over the years, approximately 100 types have been reduced and abolished. There is no surcharge on land tax, but due to the complexity of the names, a land survey has been conducted. In the counties where the survey has been completed, a cultivated land tax is levied at a tax rate of approximately 2/1000 of the land price. Recently, in order to rectify the groups, the counties have no funds to handle it, so a group fund of one time the regular tax is levied in addition to the regular tax, for a total of 4/1000.

▲ Xinjiang Province: Xinjiang Province is located in a remote western border area. Due to the frequent wars in recent years, the finances are chaotic. When the National Financial Conference was held this year, the Xinjiang Provincial Government sent representatives to attend by telegram. Now that the internal chaos has been quelled, the issue of financial reform can be gradually reorganized.

▲ Beiping City: Most of the various taxes in Beiping City follow the old system of the Capital Engineering and Patrol Donation Bureau. Now, in accordance with the financial plan, it has been decided to abolish all 13 types, including tooth tax and livestock tax, totaling more than 240,000 yuan, from November 1st. It is limited to be reorganized clearly within the year.

▲ Shanghai City: Shanghai is the most prosperous commercial area in the country. Municipal construction is progressing with the times. The expenditure in the 22nd year included a debt fee of 2,101,620 yuan. As for the tax portion, from the 23rd year, the names such as busy Cao will be abolished, and they will all be renamed land tax, divided into two types: regular and supplementary. The supplementary tax of Baoshan County exceeds one percent of the regular tax, and it has been reduced separately. There are no excessive or miscellaneous taxes in the various donations and fees collected in the urban area. It has entered the right track.

▲ Nanjing City: Nanjing City is a model area, and all constructions are waiting to be carried out. The revenue is only more than 2.9 million, while the expenditure reaches more than 4.8 million, with a huge debt. After this financial conference, in addition to the rice grain 4/1000 tax, which was abolished in October of last year, the remaining 13 types of existing house tax, car tax, deed tax, and tooth tax have all been revised separately by the municipal government, or changed to business tax, or proposed to be abolished.

▲ Qingdao City: Qingdao has been actively managed since it was recovered by our country and has become a large port on the northern coast. The city's revenue reaches more than 4.88 million yuan, and the construction is becoming more and more perfect. After this year's financial conference, a plan for reorganizing land tax was formulated: (1) compiling a land tax register and abolishing the agency collection system, and (2) conducting a land survey in rural areas and levying taxes on all land without grain. As for excessive and miscellaneous taxes, they have already been abolished.

▲ Weihaiwei: After Weihaiwei was recovered by us, a management commissioner's office was established to actively reorganize. Regarding taxes, such as fishing boat license fee, cargo sampan license fee, wind boat license fee of more than 200 dan, fishing boat license fee, and meat shop license fee, all four types will be abolished from October 1st of this year. The above five types of revenue, totaling 3,640 yuan, will be offset by the entire revenue of the tobacco and alcohol license tax in the area, which is 3,680 yuan. (End)

Another Robbery Case in Caojing Township 109

The Wang Changsheng family, a farmer in the 22nd district of Caojing, Punan, was robbed by five or six bandits speaking with local accents around 11 pm on the 24th of this month. They entered the house through the main gate with wooden sticks and flashlights and robbed two pieces of cloth, a leather women's jacket, two pieces of cloth clothing, and a silver chain before calmly escaping. Jiading 110

Second Installment of Land Tax Collection Begins

Starting this year, the county's land tax will be collected in accordance with the new regulations. All winter grain that was previously collected in the spring will be collected in two installments within the year. The first installment has already collected 40%. The second installment, in addition to reducing the collection by 17% due to poor harvest, will collect another 43%. The actual collection per mu is 1 jiao 5 fen 3 li 8 hao for provincial tax and 3 jiao 2 fen 1 li 1 hao for county tax. The collection will begin on the 25th and must be completed in full within two months.

Only the Jin Xingsheng family, a farmer, lives in Meiyuan Village, Huangdu. A dozen bandits went to rob them the night before, tying up Xingsheng and his wife and overturning boxes to search for cash. They robbed more than 30 yuan in cash, five dou of white rice, one shi of soybeans, and chicken and meat. Finally, they also stripped off the clothes worn by Xingsheng and his wife. Suzhou

County Government Executes Six Bandits by Firing Squad 113

The cases of robbery at Tang's house at No. 8 Xima Pond inside Xie Fengmen, and at Ma Chenji Tugao Store in Bifengfang Alley, Suzhou City, were solved by the Public Security Bureau's detective team, which arrested the main culprits Zhang Shaoding and others, a total of nine people. After interrogation, they were sent to the Public Security Bureau for detention. The county government presented the case to the provincial government for approval. Except for Liu Xueyi, Liu Decheng, and Zhang Shaowu, Zhang Shaoding, Wang Kesheng, Li Mengbai, Xu Yangmin, Jiang Juwu, and Zhang Shaoquan were sentenced to death. Using Bad Checks to Induce and Rape a Young Woman 114

Lu Wanqiu, a 19-year-old girl from Jiading, was studying at the Shanghai College on Jiaozhou Road, Shanghai. She was beautiful and had been betrothed to Wang Dazhi, a primary school teacher in Yangzhou. After the summer vacation this year, she owed 30 yuan in tuition fees to the school, and the current semester's food and other fees had not been paid either. She repeatedly urged her family to send money, and as a result, she only received 50 yuan, which was not enough to cover the expenses. A female classmate, Pan, promised to lend her money, so Lu took a train from Shanghai to Kunshan last month, planning to take a boat to Taicang to borrow money from Pan. Unexpectedly, she met a man named Pan Daochang at the pier. After learning the reason, Pan generously offered to lend money to Lu, advising her not to bother with the journey. So, they returned to Shanghai together. He gave her a bad check for 30 yuan, and then induced Lu to stay at the Public Security Hostel on Simalu for several days. Then, they returned to Kunshan together. Later, Lu realized that Pan already had a wife and could not help but feel resentful. She planned to commit suicide by lying on the tracks but was stopped by Pan. Later, Lu was introduced by Pan to Yu Huichun, a friend who runs the Wulin Hostel on Wumalu, Shanghai, to live with. Yu was 39 years old, from Suzhou, and not handsome. Recently, Yu and Lu returned to Suzhou together and rented a house along the river to live together. The girl's mother found out and took the two of them to the police station and sent them to the local court for interrogation and detention.

Hangzhou

Danger at the Hangzhou Seawall: Workers Dispatched to Rescue 116

According to a telegram from the Hangzhou Seawall Project Office to the Zhejiang Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau, the Shazimo No. 4 stone seawall in the Xuanwei section of the project is in danger because the sand on the beach outside the seawall has accumulated too high, causing the southern tide to impact it in a direction completely different from before. The strip stones on the first and second beaches were impacted by the tide, becoming chaotic and disorganized. The seawall body is drifting outward, and the soil behind the seawall is sinking a lot, creating a dangerous situation. Please find a way to dispatch workers to rescue it. In addition to reporting to the department, the bureau immediately dispatched workers to build the first and second beaches to protect the seawall body. At the same time, it plans to build a submerged dam to defend against the southern tide, and a surveying team was organized to measure the changes in the riverbed and beach in order to fundamentally reorganize it.

Suicide in Hangzhou Due to Economic Pressure 117

Sheng Yuanbo, a 22-year-old man from Huzhou, worked in a silk factory. Recently, due to the decline in business, he felt the pain of economic pressure, which led to discord with his family and suffered a lot of stimulation. He came to Hangzhou and stayed at No. 31 Hubin Hotel, where he secretly bought opium and swallowed it at 3 pm to commit suicide. At 9 pm, the waiter discovered him lying stiff on the bed with only a breath left. There were two letters on the table, indicating suicide. He was rushed to the hospital for treatment and is no longer in danger of death.

Stability in the Financial Market 118

Banking Sector Also Hates Rumormongers

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the silver issue, malicious people in the city have recently spread rumors to profit. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance specially instructed the banking and money industries yesterday not to easily believe rumors and to strictly investigate those who spread rumors. Chairman Chiang also made an important speech on this matter at the same time. As a result, the rumors in the city's financial market subsided yesterday morning, and people's hearts were stabilized. According to a magnate in the city's banking sector, malicious people have recently spread rumors to profit, which has occurred from time to time. The banking sector also believes that the news reported is inaccurate and that the wording of the reports these days is similar, with the heading "News from the Banking Sector," which is regrettable.

The Tongxi Section of the Longhai Railway to Officially Open on New Year's Day 119

China Merchants Bureau to Handle Lian-Yue Joint Transport

According to the Central News Agency, the western section of the Longhai Railway has now been completed. Eight passenger and freight trains were first opened yesterday, and it is scheduled to officially open on New Year's Day next year. The joint transport of goods at various stations also began yesterday. The China Merchants Bureau is scheduled to implement the Lian-Yungang to Guangzhou joint transport line today. The details are explored as follows:

Yesterday's Opening

Since construction began on the western section of the Longhai Railway this spring, progress has been very rapid. By October 10, it reached Lintong and was opened to traffic first. The section of the project from Tonglin to Xi'an was only completed the other day and opened to traffic yesterday. Two ordinary passenger trains, two special passenger trains, two freight trains, and two passenger-freight mixed trains will be operated every day. At the same time, responsible and water-land joint transport will be handled, and it is scheduled to officially open to traffic on New Year's Day.

Stations Along the Way

The road from Tongguan to Lintong has nine stations: Quandian, Huayin, Xiaying, Liuzhi, Huazhou, Shishui, Weinan, Lingkou, and Xinfengzhen. The road from Lintong to Xi'an has two stations: Yaocun and Baqiao, with a total length of 132 kilometers. The eastern section of the road from Haizhou Lianyungang to Tongguan is 916 kilometers long, and the entire line is 1,048 kilometers long, which is a trunk line from the western to eastern parts of our country, with Lianyungang as its throughput port.

China Merchants Joint Transport

The state-run China Merchants Bureau was the earliest to handle water and land joint transport with the Longhai Railway. As the western section of the road progressed, passenger and freight water and land joint transport was already handled to Xi'an. The bureau is now opening a Lianyungang to Guangzhou joint transport line. The Gongping vessel was dispatched to Haizhou yesterday and will load goods there today and sail directly to Guangzhou, stopping only in Shanghai on the way.

Sun Ke Will Soon Go to Beiping 120

To Go North After Meeting Wang Chonghui

Dr. Wang Chonghui, a member of the Central Committee, went to Zhejiang the other day and was originally scheduled to return to Shanghai yesterday morning, but he stayed behind due to matters. According to those around him, Wang will definitely come to Shanghai in the middle of this week. Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, is waiting for Wang in Shanghai. The Central, China and Communications Banks to Release $10 Million Immediately 123

To be used by silver and money exchange houses who are members of the reserve pools for mortgage loans

If needed, the three banks can allocate more funds at any time.

Xin Sheng News Agency reports: "Since the shortage of silver in Shanghai, the money market has become tight. Yesterday, the interest rate on foreign exchange interbank loans rose again to 40%. The Silver and Money Exchange Houses Association is doing its utmost to stabilize the financial situation. Considering that the combined reserves of the Banking Association Reserve Committee and the Money Exchange Reserve Pool are over $100 million, but consist of real estate deeds and securities, the Association has requested the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications to allocate funds to member banks and money shops for temporary collateral use as a precautionary measure.

The Three Banks Undertake the Task

The Chairman of the Banking Association, Chen Guangfu, and the Chairman of the Money Exchange Association, Qin Runqing, in order to regulate the financial market, consulted with the Director-General of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank, Xi Demao, the General Manager of the Bank of China, Zhang Gongquan, and the General Manager of the Bank of Communications, Tang Shoumin, to allocate funds to banks and money shops for temporary collateral use. It has been decided to provisionally allocate $10 million, with the Central Bank undertaking $5 million, and the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications each undertaking $2.5 million.

To be Implemented Immediately

It is stipulated that the 65 member money shops belonging to the Money Exchange Association Reserve Pool and the 38 banks belonging to the Banking Association Reserve Committee can, from today onwards, mortgage real estate deeds, properties, securities (including stocks, government bonds, and treasury bills), raw gold, and raw silver to the above-mentioned two reserve institutions, which can then turn to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications to mortgage for cash.

The Central Bank Takes Charge

The Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are entrusting the Central Bank to handle the $10 million in cash allocated to regulate the financial market. The President of the Central Bank, Kong Xiangxi, has instructed the Director-General of the Business Bureau, Xi Demao, to be responsible for the handling. The mortgage loans are of a temporary nature and will be stopped when the money market eases next spring. The interest rate will be 7-8%, to be determined based on the foreign exchange interbank lending rate on the day.

Additional Allocations at Any Time

A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency visited the Chairman of the Money Exchange Association, Qin Runqing, yesterday morning. According to him, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications have provisionally allocated $10 million in cash to regulate the financial market. Although the specific amounts for banks and money shops have not been specified, it is generally $5 million for each. The interest rate is from 7-8%, to be determined at any time and will be implemented from today. If the total amount required by banks and money shops exceeds $10 million, they can negotiate with the three banks to increase the allocation. This measure is actually a precaution.

Ample Reserves

As of now, Shanghai's silver reserves total approximately $30 million. The reserves of each bank and money shop are quite ample. Moreover, the assets held by the reserve institutions of the two industries are mostly reliable real estate deeds, properties, and securities. With the decision on measures to regulate the financial market with the three banks, Shanghai's financial situation is guaranteed to be secure. As for the foreign exchange interbank lending rate rising to 40%, it is a normal occurrence; it falls when supply exceeds demand, and rises when demand exceeds supply. A foreign exchange interbank lending rate of 30-40% per year is extremely common.

Besides the above official duties, I will also take the opportunity to meet with old friends and comrades in Guangdong. It has been seven years since I left Guangdong, and I have not seen my old friends for a long time. Mr. Hu Hanmin is in Hong Kong, and of course, he will be among those I visit. Political issues will inevitably be discussed. However, I believe that the unity between the comrades in the Southwest and the Central Government has recently reached a satisfactory state. When I go there, I will only talk about how to further strengthen the spirit among comrades.

Possibility of Rewarding Silver Imports

When asked about the Ministry of Finance's handling of rewarding silver imports, Kong replied that because the United States implemented a policy of raising silver prices, those seeking to profit have been exporting silver one after another. To maintain the stability of the domestic economic foundation, the government had to impose silver export taxes and equalization taxes to prevent the continued outflow of silver. Recently, some in the banking sector have suggested rewarding silver imports. I believe this can be done. If someone is willing to import silver for legitimate business investment and undergoes legal registration procedures, the government can waive silver taxes and equalization taxes when it is re-exported in the future. This is reasonable and permissible.

Continuing Discussions with the US on the Silver Issue

Kong continued, "China and the United States are continuing to exchange notes on the silver issue. Because the United States' silver policy has had a trend of impacting the Chinese economy, the Chinese government has long expressed its sincere concerns to the United States. The United States has also expressed its willingness to cooperate with China to seek financial stability in China and reduce the financial difficulties caused by the US government's implementation of the silver policy. We are currently in negotiations. China and the United States are two major countries in the Pacific, and the relations between the two countries have always been harmonious. US President Roosevelt has always expressed sympathy for our country and has a deep understanding of the Chinese situation. Therefore, I firmly believe that, based on the importance of the economic ties between China and the United States, the United States will deeply consider the close relationship between the silver issue and China and seek appropriate measures to achieve the common goal of improving the international economic environment."

Handling of the Sino-Vietnamese Trade Agreement by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs

Finally, Kong stated that the signing of the Sino-French Vietnamese trade agreement is being handled by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The French ambassador's visit the other day was regarding other matters and there were no important discussions related to the Sino-French trade agreement. It is also learned that Kong has been extremely busy with various official duties in Shanghai recently, so he will not be leaving Shanghai in the coming days. As for whether he will spend the New Year in Shanghai, Kong told reporters yesterday that he has not been able to completely confirm it.

First Batch of Guangdong Sugar Arrived Yesterday 125

Eight hundred bags transported by the Haiyuan vessel.

High quality, far superior to foreign sugar.

The Industrial and Commercial Association reports: "The Shanghai Sugar Industry Association, in view of the sharp increase in foreign sugar imports after the implementation of the new tariffs, which has greatly impacted domestic sugar, has specially dispatched Chairman Zheng Zenan to the sugar-producing areas of Guangdong for investigation a month ago to promote domestic goods and expand sales. He also contacted the Guangdong Provincial Soil Sugar Control Committee and the Guangdong Provincial National Goods Promotion Office, including Kuang Yifu, to jointly transport Guangdong sugar to Shanghai for sale, in order to prevent any leaks. According to inquiries made by reporters to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the first batch of 800 bags of Guangdong machine-made white sugar was transported to Shanghai by the Haiyuan vessel. The vessel entered the port at approximately 4:00 PM yesterday and docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf. Due to the rain, it was unable to unload, and will be stored after the warehouse is determined today or tomorrow. As for the second batch of 2,000 bags, a telegram has been sent requesting the Haili vessel to transport them, which is expected to arrive in Shanghai next week. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company attaches great importance to this large-scale transport of Guangdong sugar to Shanghai and has designated the Hua warehouse as the storage location for strict safekeeping. It is heard that the domestic sugar will be continuously transported to Shanghai for sale in the future, and that the quality of Guangdong sugar is excellent and far superior to general imported goods."

Jardine Matheson's River Steamer Ruihe Ran Aground in Zhenjiang 130

Currently Unloading Cargo

To Refloat the Ship

The British trading firm Jardine Matheson’s Changjiang liner, the Ruihe, loaded with cargo and passengers from Shanghai, was proceeding upstream on the morning of the 25th of this month. Around six or seven in the evening, the ship arrived at Zhenjiang. It was supposed to dock at the wharf to load and unload cargo and passengers, but for some reason, it suddenly ran aground on a shoal near the Taikoo lighter.

Unable to Move When it ran aground, the captain, Pace, initially intended to use full power to move the ship off the shoal and into the river. However, because the ship was fully loaded with cargo, the draft was heavy, and once it ran aground on the shoal, it could not move even a bit. At this time, the captain was overwhelmed and had no choice but to urgently inform the Zhenjiang branch and telegraph Shanghai for instructions.

Dispatching a Barge Upon Receiving the Telegram, the Shanghai office urgently telegraphed the Zhenjiang branch to quickly dispatch a barge to the site where the Ruihe was aground, quickly open the hatches and unload the cargo from the ship to reduce the load, so that the ship could float to the surface of the river, and then dispatch a tug to tow it out of danger. The ship is currently unloading cargo from the various holds, and it is expected that it will be cleared in about one or two days and then attempts will be made to rescue it from the shoal. However, passengers on board who could not wait for a long time transferred to the company’s other river steamers to proceed upstream to Wuhan. It is reported that the ship and the cargo have not been damaged.

Reason for the Jefferson's Delay 131

Due to a Fire, Undergoing Repairs in Hong Kong

The Pacific Mail liner President Jefferson of the American trading firm Dollar Steamship Lines, after arriving in Shanghai from the United States on the 12th of this month, sailed to Hong Kong and Luzon. On the afternoon of the 14th, when it was approximately one hundred nautical miles from Hong Kong, a fire suddenly broke out in the hold. Fortunately, the ship's firefighting equipment was very complete. As soon as the fire alarm was heard, all the crew members worked hard to put out the fire. Although the fire was quite intense, it was eventually extinguished. Only a portion of the cargo in the cargo hold was damaged. The shipowner telegraphed both the Hong Kong and Shanghai offices and was ordered to temporarily stop going to Luzon. It was ordered to proceed directly to Hong Kong, first unload the cargo that had been burned and damaged by water, and transfer all cargo and passengers bound for Luzon to other ships in Hong Kong for onward travel. The ship then entered the shipyard in Hong Kong for repairs and only yesterday sailed from Hong Kong to Shanghai. It is scheduled to leave Shanghai today and sail to Seattle. It will increase its speed en route in order to arrive in the United States on schedule.

The Dredging Bureau Reduces Dredging Fees 133

30 cents per cubic yard... To be implemented on New Year's Day. The Dredging Bureau issued a notice yesterday: "For the purpose of notification, the fees charged by this bureau for dredging for coastal property owners were announced on April 24th of the 22nd year of the Republic (Notice No. 234). Now, from January 1st of the 24th year, we will reduce the price to 30 cents per cubic yard (measured in the mud transport vessel, weighing approximately one ton). For those who have already contracted with this bureau for dredging, the projects after January 1st of the 24th year will also be calculated according to the above-mentioned reduced price rate. If you need an estimate of the amount of dredging, please specify the location and depth, and we can provide an estimate on your behalf. We can also handle special surveys for dredging at a low cost. If you contract with this bureau for dredging within one month, this survey fee will not be charged separately. As for whether the depth can be maintained, this bureau does not guarantee it."

Cotton Yarn Industry Improves Operations 137

Establishes a Factory Affairs Improvement Committee to Plan Everything

According to a Central News Agency report: Industrial magnate Rong Zongjing, recognizing the decline of the domestic cotton yarn industry and the dumping of foreign cotton in China, and in order to remedy the situation, previously went to various cotton-producing areas in the Northwest to conduct inspections. After returning to Shanghai, he recognized that the cotton-producing areas in the Northwest had greatly increased cotton production this year. If further improvements were made, domestic cotton yarn could be self-sufficient and there would be no need to rely on foreign cotton. At the same time, he saw that the internal equipment of the yarn factories run by Chinese businessmen was adhering to old methods and was not being improved. Therefore, he initiated the establishment of a Factory Affairs Improvement Committee, recommending nine cotton yarn industry magnates as members, with Rong Weiren as the chairman. The committee discusses matters related to the improvement of yarn factories. It has now been established and has held several meetings to discuss matters related to the internal improvement of yarn factories, such as factory management, loan interest, etc. Currently, plans are being discussed one by one.

The original text stated: "Submitting a request for the matter... In fact, firecrackers are needed for embellishment and entertainment during seasonal festivals. Such customs have been passed down for thousands of years. Historically, they have never been banned except during periods of martial law. It is true that the sound of firecrackers during seasonal festivals is familiar to the people. The so-called 'causing alarm and sudden misunderstanding' may occur during times of panic, but there is no such concern during times of peace. This is the reason why they are banned during martial law but not during times of peace. If it is said to be useless consumption, then strictly speaking, apart from cloth, silk, rice, and wheat, all other slightly luxurious items can be said to be useless consumption. The state and the people rectify customs and traditions, only using frugality to bring the people into line, and have never heard of issuing laws to impose strict prohibitions. Moreover, in terms of the consumption of firecrackers, they are only occasionally set off during weddings, funerals, celebrations, and seasonal festivals. In terms of the degree of consumption, it is far below that of luxurious items. Considering the recently popular imported consumer goods, the loss of money and the consumption of people's minds are a hundred times greater than that of firecrackers. There are occasional local people who earnestly advise against them, but the responsible authorities, concerned with tax revenue, issue documents to protect them. In all these situations, the details are seen in public reports. Only the single item of firecrackers is worried about excessively, prohibiting their use, and even detaining and fining people. Is this the way of public impartiality and forgiveness? The Book of History says, 'Government lies in nourishing the people.' Now that all industries are declining, the government is limited by its financial resources and cannot broadly plan livelihoods for the common people. How can it make so many changes, causing those who already have jobs to be driven into unemployment? Even if these unemployed workers can all endure cold and hunger and not mistakenly take the path of banditry, leading to a social crisis, but to apply the ancient saying of 'if one man is not provided for, the blame rests with the ruler,' can one be without guilt? In summary, if this action is taken, it will only add countless unemployed industrial and commercial workers to Shanghai, causing a hundred harms and no benefits. Due to our responsibilities, we dare to present this petition. We earnestly request your Bureau to review and consult with the Public Security Bureau to withdraw the order banning firecrackers in order to maintain the vitality of the industry. We await your urgent instructions. Respectfully submitted."

Cattle and Sheep Trade Association Submits to the Health Bureau Requesting the Lifting of the Cattle Ban 141

Offers Six Methods to Avoid Spreading Diseased Cattle

The Municipal Cattle and Sheep Trade Association, due to the Health Bureau's order to suspend the transport of cattle for two weeks, is suffering from a shortage of cattle in the city. Therefore, at 3:00 PM on the 25th, it convened a full executive committee meeting to discuss remedial measures. Sixty to seventy members attended and listened, as the matter concerned their vital interests, so the atmosphere was quite tense. After Chairman Chen Guanghai reported the reasons for the meeting, the executive committee members put forward six methods, which were submitted to the responsible authorities, requesting immediate implementation. The six methods are as follows: (1) Notify cattle dealers in various source areas that they must not purchase cattle with foot-and-mouth disease to transport to Shanghai. (2) Diseased cattle must not be transported to the French Concession for slaughter. (3) Disinfection work should be carried out in all cattle farms and cattle pens, that is, cleaning up accumulated dirt and spraying disinfectant. (4) Diseased cattle should be quarantined and raised separately. (5) Diseased cattle should be slaughtered and inspected first. (6) The trains transporting cattle should be disinfected.

Exhibition of Coins From Past Dynasties 152

To Be Held at the YMCA Starting Tomorrow

Mr. Yang Wenqi, a coin collector, will hold an exhibition of coins from past dynasties at the YMCA in Baxianqiao from tomorrow (29th) to the 31st. The exhibition will be open from 9:00 AM to 9:00 PM daily. The origins of the exhibition are stated as follows: Coins are relied upon by mankind for their livelihood. From ancient times to the present, they have been circulated continuously. Therefore, collecting coins used in past dynasties can create a coin history. How the culture of our country has progressed over four thousand years can also be seen from the coins of past dynasties. Tracing back to ancient times, people tied knots to record events. They traded goods for goods in the market, and there were no coins to speak of. Later, feeling the inconvenience of division, the system of currency was created. However, due to changes in the ideas of the times, the form, text, and raw materials of currency also changed accordingly. In terms of form, there are distinctions between knives, cloths, and springs. In terms of text, there are distinctions between ancient seal script, large seal script, small seal script, clerical script, regular script, running script, and cursive script. In terms of raw materials, the mixing of five metals, red copper, purple copper, bronze, white copper, iron, lead, gold, and silver also varied according to the evolution of civilization. The same knife also has differences in length, short, width, and narrowness, form, and weight. The same cloth also has differences in the flatness, sharpness, and roundness of the shoulders and feet. The same spring also has inconsistencies in the presence or absence of inner and outer rims and the squareness and roundness of the holes. The raw materials, text, size, and weight are not fixed and unchanging, which is enough for us to conduct detailed research. It is a pity that the people of our country ignore it, and unscrupulous merchants only care about profit. They have almost exhausted the most valuable coins in Chinese history for foreigners to collect. Moreover, domestic coins are destroyed to extract copper to make other utensils, so that the coins of past dynasties in my country with a unified system are difficult to find in museums, libraries, and exhibition halls in the country, which is regrettable. I have traveled extensively in Yan, Liao, Qin, and Long for more than twenty years, collecting various ancient coins everywhere. After a long time, the number has been quite large. It has long been appreciated by fellow enthusiasts. The inscriptions and rubbings compiled by Shiquan Cangquan have also received considerable criticism from contemporary appraisers. In the northwest, where the origin of our country's culture is earliest, it is still regarded as rare and valuable, so it must be cherished and valued. At a time when we are paying attention to preserving antiques, we feel that it is necessary to contribute to society. I have specially compiled, collated, and exhibited them in chronological order. I hope that you gentlemen who are interested in Chinese history and relics will come and guide me. I am very grateful. Respectfully, Yang Wenqi of Shiquan.

The Dredging Bureau's Large Mud Boat Ordered From Germany is Nearing Completion 153

Each Time It Dredges 4,000 Tons, Specially for Dredging the Shoals

The Parts Will be Assembled and Shipped to China in February of Next Year

The world's largest dredging vessel ordered by the Dredging Bureau from Germany some time ago is about to be completed, according to the bureau. The dredging vessel is scheduled to leave Germany for China in early February next year. The details are recorded below.

Dredging Plan

The Bureau believes that the shoals and reefs at the mouth of the Yangtze River, located in the center of the Yangtze River estuary, occupy a large area and obstruct traffic, so that huge seagoing vessels cannot enter the port. Even the larger vessels currently sailing in the Yangtze River and the Huangpu River must wait for the tide to rise before they can pass, otherwise they will be in danger of running aground. The Bureau's Chief Engineer, Mr. Chantrill, after years of research, has determined that most of the shoals are composed of mud. He has ordered the world's largest dredging vessel from Germany, planning to dredge on a large scale to facilitate traffic. According to Mr. Chantrill, the dredging plan for the shoals will be divided into two phases. The first phase is tentatively set for five years, and the second phase will be determined based on the work done in the first phase.

Scheduled to Ship to China

The ship was designed by Chief Engineer Chantrill and built by the Schichau shipyard in Elbing, Germany. It was agreed that the goods would be delivered in Shanghai and represented by the German company Siemens. The ship is 360 feet long and 60 feet wide. Each time, it can dredge 4,000

Afterwards, based on Zhu's confession, the police dispatched detectives to Ningbo to investigate and arrest the accomplice of the murderer. On November 18th, they finally arrested Chen Jinlan (also known as Li Jinlan, nicknamed "Snake Skin" Jinlan, 32 years old this year) in the countryside.

Transfer and Detention to Shanghai 155

The offender was escorted to the Second Special District Court, tried and sentenced to fourteen years of imprisonment. The offender did not accept the verdict and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, but the appeal was rejected. Chen still refused to accept this and appealed to the Supreme Court. Therefore, the Chen offender was detained in Cell No. 11 of the Heavy Sentence Division of the Second District Court Detention Center. Now, the Supreme Court has rendered a judgment, changing the sentence to twelve years of imprisonment. The judgment was recently sent to the Third Branch of the High Court, which dispatched police to serve it on the Chen offender. An inspection of the inner and outer iron doors showed that they were still sealed and not locked as before, making it difficult to understand the path of his escape. Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen were interrogated, and their legal representatives, Yi Hu (Fangshuo's stepmother) and Li Duofu, hired lawyers to appear in court, requesting that the charges be withdrawn and that the two girls be allowed to be taken back. The court granted this request and then proceeded to try the charges of harming family and restricting freedom. The defendant was defended by lawyers Sha Xunyi and Hu Jue. Judge Zhang Chaozuo had declared the debate closed, and the defendant was transferred to the detention center to await sentencing. The previous reports had already covered all the details. Yesterday was the date for sentencing, and Yi's family and friends all came to the court to listen. At 10:00 AM, Judge Qiu Huan Ying, acting on behalf of the First Criminal Court, ordered the police to go to the detention center to bring Yi Fangshuo to the court. The defendant's defense lawyers also arrived to await the verdict. The official briefly questioned the defendant about his age, origin, address, and occupation, and then announced the verdict: Yi Fangshuo is sentenced to three years of imprisonment for depriving others of their freedom of movement by illegal means. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be deducted from the prison term at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The charges of harming family are acquitted, and the charges of violating public morals are not accepted. After the verdict was announced, the defendant was returned to the detention center to await instructions during the appeal period. Yi's face changed drastically upon hearing the verdict, and his eyes were filled with tears. He was taken away by the police and returned to detention. Yi's family, one wife and three concubines, all covered their faces and sobbed upon hearing the verdict, and left dejectedly.

Valuable Diamond Ring Lost Case 163

Rickshaw Puller Cannot Escape the Law

Whereabouts of the Strange-Looking Man Unknown

Ma Xintian, a jewelry broker, had a diamond ring with a diamond weighing 16.75 carats. Because he wanted to sell it, he gave it to his colleague Feng Zichuan to sell on his behalf. On October 16th of this year, Feng placed the ring in his sock and went to the Yueyuli brothel on Yunnan Road to sell it. When he arrived in the alley, he suddenly could not find it. Ma found out about this and negotiated with Feng, who compensated him with 8,500 yuan. At that time, the ring was picked up by Lu Asan, a rickshaw puller from Haimen at No. 26 Qingyuan Street, Tong Yongtai. At that time, Lu was waiting in the alley because his master was playing in the brothel. Lu was overjoyed at obtaining the precious ornament and could not keep it a secret. The next day, he discussed it with his fellow townsman, Lu Ada, also a rickshaw puller, and showed him the ring for mutual admiration. However, both were doubtful and could not identify whether it was genuine or fake. They went to Haining to briefly consult with Xing Pawnshop to ask them to determine the authenticity. The pawnbroker glanced at the ring and told them that if they wanted to determine whether it was genuine or fake, it would take a considerable period of time and could not be decided hastily. The two Lus then took the ring and went to Hongxing Pawnshop on North Sichuan Road, still asking for an estimate. Wu Shangshou, the young owner of the pawnshop, used a microscope to examine the diamond and then took the ring upstairs. At this moment, a strange-looking man with a protruding lower lip suddenly walked into Hongxing and expressed his desire to buy the ring. Wu Shangshou then came downstairs and told the two Lus that if they were willing to sell it, it was worth six yuan. The two Lus refused and took the original ring back. On November 12th, Lu Asan happened to be standing in front of Tong Yongtai, looking around, when he saw Wu Shangshou walking around the area, lingering for a long time. Lu initially did not pay attention to it. That night, the strange-looking man he had seen before became an uninvited guest and visited Lu Asan, directly saying that he wanted to buy the ring. Lu said that it was inconvenient to talk in detail at this time and agreed to meet at the Hujiang Hotel the next day in the name of Chen Nianlin. When the time came, Lu went as agreed, carrying the treasure with him. Wu Shangshou also arrived and valued it at 900 yuan. The strange-looking man paid the price and took the ring, Wu left, and Lu also left with the money and shared it with Ada. More than a month passed, and the two Lus did not see the owner pursue the matter, thinking that it was safe. Unexpectedly, recently, Detective Zhang Yuanjing and Detective Cui Jinchuan of the Zhabei Police Station found out about it and immediately arrested the two Lus and questioned them about the details. The two Lus were guilty of illegally appropriating lost property and were brought to the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Judge Xiang Yinghua interrogated them. Zhang Shizhu, the lawyer of the police station, asked to punish the two defendants for the crime under Article 358 of the Criminal Code, and Detective Zhang reported the details of the investigation of the case, presenting a savings passbook with more than 600 yuan found in Lu Ada's possession as evidence. Wu Shangshou, accompanied by his lawyer Jiang Yiping, voluntarily surrendered himself. The owner, Feng Zichuan, also hired lawyer Fan Gang to appear in court, stating that Feng had already compensated Ma Xintian with 8,500 yuan, so he specifically filed a claim for damages against the two defendants, ordering them to repay 8,500 yuan. However, the strange-looking man was still unknown, and there was no way to summon him. Judge Xiang questioned the defendants one by one and ordered the two Lus to pay a bail of 1,000 yuan each. Wu Shangshou left to await further interrogation.

Liang Tongfang from Shaoxing was previously accused of selling Japanese goods in the Yue Lai South Goods Store on Guangdong Road and threatened with a bomb. However, he was careless in throwing the bomb. In addition to injuring Ding Yanzhi and other shop assistants, Liang also injured his left and right hands. The police station sent him to the First Special District Court, which sentenced Liang to six months of imprisonment with a three-year suspended sentence. Subsequently, the Public Works Department disagreed and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court. The result was still the original sentence. However, according to Liang's statement reported in various newspapers yesterday, the appeal period for this case has now passed, and the police station will no longer appeal. However, according to Mr. Wang, the lawyer of the Legal Department of the Public Works Department, he told reporters that after the Second Branch of the High Court served the judgment on the 14th of this month, the Public Works Department submitted a statement to the Second Branch of the High Court on the 17th, declaring an appeal, and rushed to draft the reasons for the appeal. The reasons have now been drafted and were submitted to the Second Branch of the High Court yesterday to be forwarded to the Supreme Court for appeal. Therefore, Liang's claim that the police station will no longer appeal is not a fact.

Drug Manufacturing Factory Found on Meibage Road 164

The Manufacturers Fled in Advance

Countless Drugs and Equipment Seized

In recent months, the public concession has cracked down on several privately established drug manufacturing facilities. However, the manufacturers are mostly resourceful and well-informed, and they often escape in advance. Therefore, these people only sacrifice drugs and manufacturing tools, while they themselves remain at large. Once the rumors subside slightly, it is not difficult to make a comeback, so that the production of drugs is still endless, and there is no hope of clearing it up. Recently, there are as many as three drug manufacturing factories set up by these people in No. 90 Lane (i.e., Xiang Kangli) on Meibage Road, Xinzha. The working hours are often late at night and extremely secretive. Even the residents in the same neighborhood cannot know. One night, Wu Changkai, a detective of the Xinzha Police Station, happened to pass by the area and smelled an unusually strong odor of opium-like morphine emanating from the windows. He knew that there must be a den of drugs in the lane, so he started investigating. After several days of investigation, he found out that there were indeed three drug dens in the lane. According to intelligence, the Baoshan police chief requested the First Special District Court to issue a search warrant. At 5:00 PM the day before, he went with Chinese and Western detectives to search each address one by one. Only in the kitchen of No. 70, a drug manufacturing factory was found. Eighteen pounds of heroin, ten large glass bottles, five vats, twenty wooden boxes, twenty-two empty alcohol cans, two small stoves, three kerosene stoves, and two basins were seized. The other two locations had already been emptied, and the manufacturers had fled without a trace. The Chinese and Western detectives then transported the seized items back to the police station. Yesterday morning, Zhang Tianyin, the lawyer of the Public Works Department, requested the First Special District Court to approve the detention of the items, awaiting the arrest of the perpetrators to be punished.

Two Bureaus Plan to Build Central Station 171

Double Track Between Shanghai and Nanxiang to Be Completed Next Month

In order to facilitate the transfer of vehicles between the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways and the Beijing-Wuhu and Tianjin-Pukou Railways, the Ministry of Railways has decided to build a central station in Beijing and has instructed the two bureaus to be responsible for planning. According to the news from the bureau, various construction matters are actively underway. The laying of double tracks on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway from Shanghai to Nanxiang to facilitate the movement of vehicles has been 80 to 90 percent completed since construction began and is expected to be completed next month. As for the full double-tracking of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, it will depend on future resources due to funding constraints. The railway is also striving to improve the equipment at each station for the safety of passengers on both railways. Mr. Huang Boqiao, the director of the bureau, was sent abroad to inspect and has been abroad for half a year. He is currently inspecting in Germany and will leave Germany to inspect Denmark, Poland, and other countries, and is scheduled to return to Shanghai from Italy in March next year.

Public Works Bureau Plans to Purchase Land to Widen Nanjing Road and Henan Road Corner 172

The parcel of land located at No. 160, the corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road, is subject to the pre-determined plan to widen the road and should be acquired, measuring one mu, two fen, and eight li. The Public Works Bureau is in consultation with Mrs. Hardoon, the landowner, regarding this matter. However, the Bureau has not been able to agree to the compensation demanded by the landowner. This case has now been submitted to the Land Committee for arbitration.

It has been investigated that the building located at the corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road had an incident on March 20th of this year at around 6:00 PM, where bricks and plaster collapsed, injuring several pedestrians on Nanjing Road. Traffic on that section was significantly hampered for several days thereafter. The Public Works Bureau immediately sent personnel to inspect the building, and the owner also arranged for repairs. However, this parcel of land was already designated for acquisition in the 1926 plan, measuring one mu, two fen, and eight hao, in preparation for widening the road. The land had long belonged to Mr. Hardoon. If this acquisition is implemented, it would greatly benefit traffic flow. However, it must wait until the parcel of land at No. 162 further east is also acquired according to plan and aligned with the Electricity Company's building before the overall traffic flow of Nanjing Road can be significantly improved.

Two Suspects Arrested for Shooting and Killing an Indian Constable 173

Yesterday, Separate Interrogation Was Conducted by the First Special Court

Both Suspects Shifted Blame in Hopes of Evading Responsibility

Indian Constable No. 258 of the Yangshupu Police Station was fatally shot in a vital area near a foreign-owned sock factory on Hejian Road at 10:45 PM on the 9th of this month. The perpetrators were at large. The day before yesterday at around 10:00 AM, Chinese Detective Liu Wenzao and Western Detective White apprehended a suspect named Zhou Hongtian from Taizhou at the corner of Xizang Road and Avenue Edward VII. Upon interrogation, they learned that an accomplice, Wang Jinsheng (also from Taizhou), resided at No. 267 Huangpu Road in the French Concession. Subsequently, he was also apprehended on Rue du Consulat and both were taken to the Yangshupu Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Division of the First Special Court for separate interrogation. Mr. Li Zhishan, the lawyer for the Public Works Bureau, stated that in their statements at the police station, the two defendants shifted blame to each other, both claiming Wang was the perpetrator, while Wang claimed that Zhou initiated the act and that he held the gun, which bore the inscription "Shanghai." It has been verified that the gun belonged to Luo Xingfa, who has already been summoned and the gun is currently in the custody of the French police for examination. It will be presented to the court at the next hearing. At the time of the incident, a gray bowler hat was found lying on the roadside nearby. Wang claimed that Zhou was wearing it at the time and threw it on the ground after the crime. The case is requested to be postponed, etc. The hat was presented for inspection. When questioned, Zhou Hongtian claimed that he was invited by Wang Jinsheng to visit the area and they first had a meager meal in a lane in nearby Huaxingfang. Afterwards, they walked together to Linqing Road, where they encountered the Indian constable, who stopped them for inspection. He then took out a gun and opened fire, firing five or six shots. Upon seeing this, he immediately fled and returned to his home at No. 2 Dexingfang, Yangshupu. The next day at around 2:00 PM, Wang came to his house and told him to go to the French Concession.

In his statement, Wang Jinsheng said that at 5:00 PM that afternoon, he met Zhou at the entrance of the Great World and told him to visit a friend in Yangshupu. While walking near the scene of the incident, they encountered an Indian constable. Zhou immediately pulled out a handgun with the inscription "Shanghai" and tried to fire it at the constable. He told him not to, but Zhou did not listen and fired one shot at the constable. He was frightened and immediately fled back to his home in the French Concession. The next day, Zhou came to his place and told him to stay at the Yi Kai small hotel near Chenjia Wooden Bridge. The presented hat was indeed the one he was wearing at the time and abandoned after firing the shot, etc. When questioned, Zhou firmly maintained that Wang was the main culprit. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered both defendants to be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing for further investigation.
